1 About this Document
1.1 Goal of This Document
This document contains all architecture information for ISCP SATA 3.0 Controller.
1.2 Audience
This document is a feature HAS, which describes what the ISCP SATA 3.0 feature is and how it works, to be consumed primarily by the
design and validation teams.
The information in this document is also intended for SoC design team that is using ISCP SATA 3.0 SIP. See section Supported Projects
for projects that use SATA SIP.
1.3 Supported Projects
This document supports the following projects at the listed RTL maturity level.
Table: RTL Support Level for SoC Projects (source)
Project Name IP Maturity Level
All SoCs (Multi) 1.0-v0
ADP-S 1.0-v0
ALL 1.0-v1
BXT_P 1.0-v0
CNP_LP 1.0-v0

TGP-LP 1.0-v3

The following table provides a history of revisions made to this IP.
Table: SATA Revision History (source)
Rev
Description Rev Date
Number
Initial draft based on 2013 HAS 1.0 dated 3/19/14.
0.5 3/19/2014
NVMe Remapping support by adding register RUN register in ABAR offset A8h.
Register section changes:
Change the NVMEBDF[15:0] in RUN to NVMEDF[7:0].
Add offset $TSO to all the MMIO register in MXTBA space.
Add offset $TPO to all the MMIO register in MXPBA space.
Add the descrioption in Config offset 0h: When the MMIO RUN.RUNE=1, read access to this double-word register is
0.6 return with UR. 4/18/2014
Add SATAGC.DOSERRD.
Change MXT.TO attribute from RO to RWO.
Change MXP.PBAO attribute from RO to RWO.
IOSF Sideband Servces section change:
Add the “and SATAGC.DOSERRD=0” for all the condition to trigger do_serr.
Typo correction on the reset description for MFID.MID.
Incorporate the feedback on HAS 0.7 review from CNP. This include (1) removal of the notion of SATA PSF, (2) PCH PSF
not shadowing the new register to support NVMe Remapping but instead use the 2nd SATA Fabric Decoder to route the
downstream completion, (3) etc
0.7RC1 Mentioned that PxCMD.ESP is not reset by HBA reset 4/29/2014
Update BXT-P clocks and reset information.
Update BXT-P block diagram.
Update BXT-P VISA structure
Add the Security Check List
0.7 Released as SIP HAS 0.7 5/20/2014
Update the GHC_CAP.NP register to change no port value from 7h to Fh.
Update the SIR register map table to tag those DFx register with * to mean non-State-Retention-flop register
Add note in MXT.TO and MXP.PBAO that BIOS shall ensure the program value to be within the space of the
MXTBA/MXPBA.
Add PTM5[23:16] as the Link Active State Status per 8 ports.
Update the SPGIO Waveform in Enclosure Management that show the 24-bit bit stream. This 24-bit diagram somehow
was replaced with the 18-bit version.
0.8RC1 5/21/2014
Add 2 bank SAI Access Control policy register in Config offset 40h-4Fh to protect the Config/MMIO/IO Space due to VTd
security requirement.
All the tables missing the bookmark. Hence reinsert the table caption to rebuild the table content.
Add the RST’s RAID DID info into DID sub section.
Reintroduce BAR2 and BAR3 as workaround to RST issue.
Update the description for MAP.SPD[7:6] to remove the “/RO” attribute which depends on the fuse, soft strap and GP pin.
This is to match the design. The HAS “/RO” behavior was editorial left over since 2011 HAS rev 0.4!

1.00 Update TGPLP LZ Table to change PME output as wire instead of SBI Message to reuse the BXT_P flow in TGPLP where 2/17/2017
SATA sits in VNNAON and it use the PME wire to wake PMC out from VNN Removed state. Refer to PCR 1405427178.

onward. Description update only. No HW change.

bridge the Gap from modPHY to SNPS PHY.
SUN. Corrected CTM3.CWCIBRUMIN from “equal or larger… then invalidate” to “less… then invalidate”
Support ADP_S PCR 1507067537 by adding CTM2.VGCVCI
Update Section 17 Safety, that SATA is not FUSA Safety IP and hence that Section is N/A.

3 Functional Description
SATA host controller is a PCI device function that support the AHCI host controller modes. It can support up to 8 SATA ports. The
subsequent sections in this section provide high level micro-architectural building blocks which made up the SIP SATA controller. The
next section will provide the programming model employed by the SIP SATA controller.
3.1 High Level SATA Controller Architecture
The overall architecture of the Serial ATA (SATA) interface is depicted in Figure: Block Diagram of a SATA Architecture. The layering of
the functions facilitates the design of the resultant logic blocks by the designers.
1. The physical layer is located at the lowest level of the interface and responsible for generating the actually transmitted signal over the
SATA interconnect and for deciphering received analogue signals. The specification also specifies the cables and connectors, but this
is outside the scope of this document.
2. The link layer, which is above the physical layer, defines the encoding for data being transmitted. It also defines the control signals and
protocol that reliably transmits packets of data between transmitter and receiver.
3. The transport layer, which is above the link layer, defines the format and function of data structures that are exchanged between the
transmitter and receiver. The data structures are also known as Frame Information Structures (FISes).
4. The command layer defines the sequences of FISes that need to be exchanged to support all the command protocols that are defined
in the existing Parallel ATA specification.
5. The SATA specification also assumes the presence of a host controller interface and makes reference to a set of registers that are
central to the existing Parallel ATA (PATA) implementation in the SATA specification. These programming registers, which is also
referred to as “taskfile” registers, are not compulsory in implementing the host controller. However, the operation of the transport and
command layers in providing a backward compatible software solution centers around manipulation of the “taskfile” registers for
legacy software applications.
6. The application layer operate in AHCI host bus adaptor (HBA) mode.
Figure: Block Diagram of a SATA Architecture
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 11/242
=== PAGE 12 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
The SIP SATA controller can be broken into multiple major building blocks, i.e. VRUNIT, VSAUNIT, PLPUNIT and PLUNIT.
Figure: Another View of the SATA Architecture Breakdown shows the basic building blocks of the SIP SATA controller. The VSAUNIT
implements the command/DMA, transport and link layer of the SATA specification, mentioned earlier. The VRunit is the router and
configuration block for the SATA interface. It is primarily responsible for claiming, forwarding and completing non-port-specific memory,
configuration and I/O transactions for SATA cluster. The PLPUNIT contains the per port interfacing logic for providing part of the PHY
layer control. The PLUNIT contains common PHY module control logic, e.g. PLL related configuration control.
The physical control service (PCS) and modular PHY (MOD-PHY) module combined represents the PHY layer implementation. It is
outside the scope of this document.
Figure: Another View of the SATA Architecture Breakdown
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 12/242

3.2 Power Up Sequence
Figure: SATA SIP Power Up Sequence - SATA PLL to Use External refclk and Figure: SATA SIP Power Up Sequence - SATA PLL to Use
Internal refclk show the power up sequence of the SATA cluster. The difference between these figures is the SATA PLL source. The flow
is a bit different between both because MOD-PHY’s default refclk selection is the external refclk. This selection bit is in the MOD-PHY’s
IOSF SB register. To change the selection to the internal refclk, the SoC needs to ensure that the IOSF SB interface is up and the
selection is done, prior to the deassertion of MOD-PHY’s i_cmnreset_l (that is, bb_rst_b, which is the IOSF PRIM interface reset).
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 18/242
=== PAGE 19 ===

Figure: SATA SIP Power Up Sequence - SATA PLL to Use External refclk
Figure: SATA SIP Power Up Sequence - SATA PLL to Use Internal refclk

6.1.1.2.1 IOSF Reset Assertion and Deassertion Requirement
The two signals, prim_rst_b and side_rst_b, are used to reset the agents. Both signals will assert at the same time asynchronously, and
deassert synchronously, unless the primary and sideband interfaces are in separate power wells.[RA383] The side_rst_b may deassert
before prim_rst_b. This is done when sideband endpoints in the system are used to initialize private registers in agents before the
system is released from reset. The component designer must ensure that side_rst_b is deasserted for a sufficient time before
prim_rst_b is deasserted. An agent with a sideband endpoint must ensure the sideband endpoint can generate. Completions while
prim_rst_b is asserted.[RA384].
Above is the excerpt from IOSF Spec 1.0. The following figure shows the waveform per that IOSF that require both bb_rst_b and
side_rst_b to assert at the same time. There is no bb_rst_b Reset Warn needed if SoC compliant to this behavior.
Figure: bb_rst_b and side_rst_b Assert Together (without bb_rst_b Reset Warn)
If the SoC delays the side_rst_b assertion, then bb_rst_b Reset Warn flow is needed to quiescent the sideband bus cleanly prior to the
bb_rst_b assertion (the following figure). Refer to the Ingress Reset Warn message on the Sideband Interface for more detail.
Figure: side_rst_b Assert Later than bb_rst_b (with bb_rst_b Reset Warn)
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 25/242
=== PAGE 26 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
If the SoC delays the side_rst_b assertion, but there is no bb_rst_b Reset Warn flow prior to the bb_rst_b assertion, then the abrupt
bb_rst_b assertion may cause SIP to hang the sideband interface by sending malformed message or incomplete message (the
following figure).
Figure: side_rst_b Assert Later than bb_rst_b (without bb_rst_b Reset Warn)

6.1.2.1.3 Clock Tree Requirement
Each SIP lane talks to each MOD-PHY lane synchronously using 1 per port clocks, i.e. pclk_hbpclk#. There is a requirement to sync all
these per lane clocks, due to the port staggering logic requirement. SoC CTS needs to ensure that the clock tree buffers are added in
core logic to match MOD-PHY clock tree insertion delay. (See the following figure.)
Figure: TBC Clock Tree

6.1.3.2.1 IOSF Reset Assertion and Deassertion Requirement
The two signals, prim_rst_b and side_rst_b, are used to reset the agents. Both signals will assert at the same time asynchronously, and
deassert synchronously, unless the primary and sideband interfaces are in separate power wells.[RA383] The side_rst_b may deassert
before prim_rst_b. This is done when sideband endpoints in the system are used to initialize private registers in agents before the
system is released from reset. The component designer must ensure that side_rst_b is deasserted for a sufficient time before
prim_rst_b is deasserted. An agent with a sideband endpoint must ensure the sideband endpoint can generate. Completions while
prim_rst_b is asserted.[RA384]
Above is the excerpt from IOSF Spec 1.0. The following figure shows the waveform per that IOSF that require both bb_rst_b and
side_rst_b to assert at the same time. There is no bb_rst_b Reset Warn needed if SoC compliant to this behavior.
Figure: bb_rst_b and side_rst_b assert together (without bb_rst_b Reset Warn)
If the SoC delays the side_rst_b assertion, then bb_rst_b Reset Warn flow is needed to quiescent the sideband bus cleanly prior to the
bb_rst_b assertion (see the following figure). Refer to the Ingress Reset Warn message on the Sideband Interface for more detail.
Figure: side_rst_b assert later than bb_rst_b (with bb_rst_b Reset Warn)
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 37/242
=== PAGE 38 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
If SoC delay the side_rst_b assertion, but there is no bb_rst_b Reset Warn flow prior to the bb_rst_b assertion, then the abrupt bb_rst_b
assertion may cause SIP to hang the sideband interface by sending malformed message or incomplete message (see the following
figure).
Figure: side_rst_b assert later than bb_rst_b (without bb_rst_b Reset Warn)

6.1.4.1.3 Clock Tree Requirement
Each SIP lane talks to each MOD-PHY lane synchronously using 1 per port clocks, i.e. pclk_hbpclk#. There is a requirement to sync all
these per lane clocks, due to the port staggering logic requirement. SoC CTS needs to ensure that the clock tree buffers are added in
core logic to match MOD-PHY clock tree insertion delay. (See the following figure.)
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 42/242

6.1.4.2.1 IOSF Reset Assertion and Deassertion Requirement
The two signals, prim_rst_b and side_rst_b, are used to reset the agents. Both signals will assert at the same time asynchronously, and
deassert synchronously, unless the primary and sideband interfaces are in separate power wells.[RA383] The side_rst_b may deassert
before prim_rst_b. This is done when sideband endpoints in the system are used to initialize private registers in agents before the
system is released from reset. The component designer must ensure that side_rst_b is deasserted for a sufficient time before
prim_rst_b is deasserted. An agent with a sideband endpoint must ensure the sideband endpoint can generate. Completions while
prim_rst_b is asserted.[RA384]
Above is the excerpt from IOSF Spec 1.0. The following figure shows the waveform per that IOSF that require both bb_rst_b and
side_rst_b to assert at the same time. There is no bb_rst_b Reset Warn needed if the SoC is compliant to this behavior.
Figure: bb_rst_b and side_rst_b Assert Together (without bb_rst_b Reset Warn)
If the SoC delays the side_rst_b assertion, then bb_rst_b Reset Warn flow is needed to quiescent the sideband bus cleanly prior to the
bb_rst_b assertion (Figure: side_rst_b Assert Later than bb_rst_b (with bb_rst_b Reset Warn)). Refer to the Ingress Reset Warn message
on the Sideband Interface for more detail.
Figure: side_rst_b Assert Later than bb_rst_b (with bb_rst_b Reset Warn)
If the SoC delays the side_rst_b assertion, but there is no bb_rst_b Reset Warn flow prior to the bb_rst_b assertion, then the abrupt
bb_rst_b assertion may cause SIP to hang the sideband interface by sending malformed message or incomplete message (see the
following figure).
Figure: side_rst_b Assert Later than bb_rst_b (without bb_rst_b Reset Warn)

6.4 Clocking Assumptions
Describe. If this section does not apply, enter “Not applicable to this IP”.

6.5 PRIM_CLK_FREQ
SATA Controller use the prim_clk in 4 timers where 3 of them need to meet the Industrial SATA Spec and one of them to meet the SATA
HAS Spec. Since different SoC may have different frequency of prim_clk, SATA SIP provide a param called PRIM_CLK_FREQ for SoC to
confirgure. The param PRIM_CLK_FREQ only support 5 values, i.e. 100, 125, 133, 266 and 137.14 MHz.
Some SoC may not have the exact prim_clk frequency supported by this param PRIM_CLK_FREQ. The rule of thumb is to configure the
param PRIM_CLK_FREQ to a value larger than the actual prim_clk frequency. For example:
ICP PCH has the actual prim_clk frequency of 128 MHz but configure the param PRIM_CLK_FREQ to 133 MHz (Case #2b in Table:
Param PRIM_CLK_FREQ and Actual prim_clk Frequency)
EBG has the actual prim_clk frequency of 248 MHz but configure the param PRIM_CLK_FREQ to 266 MHz (Case #3b in Table: Param
PRIM_CLK_FREQ and Actual prim_clk Frequency)
Table: Definition of Param PRIM_CLK_FREQ (source)
IOSF Primary Clock Frequency
Parameter Supported Parameter Value Encoding
(MHz)
IOSF Primary clock frequency (in Mhz). Clock frequency of IOSF primary interface, SATA link clock
(st_lgclk) is 2x synchronous of this primary clock.
100,

8.1.1.1 IOSF Reset Assertion and Deassertion Requirement
The two signals, prim_rst_b and side_rst_b, are used to reset the agents. Both signals will assert at the same time asynchronously, and
deassert synchronously, unless the primary and sideband interfaces are in separate power wells.[RA383] The side_rst_b may deassert
before prim_rst_b. This is done when sideband endpoints in the system are used to initialize private registers in agents before the
system is released from reset. The component designer must ensure that side_rst_b is deasserted for a sufficient time before
prim_rst_b is deasserted. An agent with a sideband endpoint must ensure the sideband endpoint can generate. Completions while
prim_rst_b is asserted.[RA384].
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 46/242
=== PAGE 47 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
Above is the excerpt from IOSF Spec 1.0. The following figure shows the waveform per that IOSF that require both bb_rst_b and
side_rst_b to assert at the same time. There is no bb_rst_b Reset Warn needed if SoC compliant to this behavior.
Figure: bb_rst_b and side_rst_b assert together (without bb_rst_b Reset Warn)
If SoC delay the side_rst_b assertion, then bb_rst_b Reset Warn flow is needed to quiescent the sideband bus cleanly prior to the
bb_rst_b assertion (see the following figure). Refer to the Ingress Reset Warn message on the Sideband Interface for more detail.
Figure: side_rst_b assert later than bb_rst_b (with bb_rst_b Reset Warn)
If SoC delay the side_rst_b assertion, but there is no bb_rst_b Reset Warn flow prior to the bb_rst_b assertion, then the abrupt bb_rst_b
assertion may cause SIP to hang the sideband interface by sending malformed message or incomplete message (see the following
figure).
Figure: side_rst_b assert later than bb_rst_b (without bb_rst_b Reset Warn)

10 Register Description
SATA Host Controller has registers in PCI Config space, MMIO space, and IO Space. These registers are accessible from both the IOSF
Primary interface and Sideband Interface. These three spaces are protected from access from cycle of certain SAI (SAI of different VM)
from accessing these space to fulfill VTd security requirement, by using the group 0 SAI policy register. Refer to G0SAIPOLCTRL and
G0SAIPOLAC register description.
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 47/242
=== PAGE 48 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
10.1 Configuration Registers
All of the SATA configuration registers are in the core well. All registers not mentioned are reserved.
NOTE: All configuration registers are reset by function level reset (FLR) unless specified otherwise explicitly.
When the SATA host controller enters the IP Accessible power gating state, all Configuration registers’ contexts are kept, unless
explicitly specified otherwise. Configuration registers for which the context is not kept are reset.

Implementation Note (to be removed from EDS):
List of fuses:
FFSATA0p0 = Disable Port 0 Gen 3 Speed (1 = disable Gen3 speed)
FFSATA0p1 = Disable Port 1 Gen 3 Speed (1 = disable Gen3 speed)
FFSATA0p2 = Disable Port 2 Gen 3 Speed (1 = disable Gen3 speed)
FFSATA0p3 = Disable Port 3 Gen 3 Speed (1 = disable Gen3 speed)
FFSATA0p4 = Disable Port 4 Gen 3 Speed (1 = disable Gen3 speed)
FFSATA0p5 = Disable Port 5 Gen 3 Speed (1 = disable Gen3 speed)
FFSATA0p6 = Disable Port 6 Gen 3 Speed (1 = disable Gen3 speed)
FFSATA0p7 = Disable Port 7 Gen 3 Speed (1 = disable Gen3 speed)
Combination with FFSATA5 and FFSATA3:
‘00’ - No RAID, No Optane (note on the impact to the PFB register)
‘01’ - No RAID, Optane Only (note: Since KBP_H)
‘10’ - Reserved
‘11’ - Premium (RAID w/ Optane, or RAID w/o Optane, depends on LPCDID)
FFSATA7 = SATA 4-Port All Master Configuration (1 = disable port 2 and 3); meant for both desktop and mobile SKUs
FFSATA8 = SATA 4-Port Configuration (1 = disable port 1 and 3); meant for mobile SKUs
FFDM = Enable Desktop/Mobile feature (0 = desktop; 1 = mobile which does not change SATA port SKU)
FFSATA1 = Reserved and not used
FFSATA2 = Reserved and not used
FFSATA4 = Reserved and not used
FFSATA6 = Reserved and not used

Note to BIOS: If all SATA ports are assigned to PCIe/USB3/SSIC lanes instead of SATA ports, then BIOS should have the SATA
controller Device Function disabled. Refer to section Disabling SATA Host Controller (PCI Function Disable) for controller disable
flow in order to achieve max power savings.
16-bit Device ID consist of upper 12-bit and lower 4-bit. The lower 4-bit is decided based on some config bits and fuses as shown in
the table. The upper 12-bit, i.e. strap[15:4] in the table consist of upper 9-bit and lower 3-bit where is upper 9-bit is from DW#2 bit
[31:23] of the SetID message received on IOSF Sideband, while the lower 3-bit is the strap_creg_devid[2:0] in SATA host controller
wrapper input pin. This definition is described in section Device ID Assignment.

10.1.1.11 Offset 10h: MXTBA -MSI-X Table Base Address
This BAR is used to allocate 32K, 16K or 8K Memory space for the MSI-X Table. The Memory space size is determined by BIOS by
making bit-14 and bit-13 Read-Only ‘1’ or Read-Write ‘0’ based on SATAGC.MSS[1:0].
NOTE: If Fabric Decoding scheme is used, this register is shadowed by the Fabric Decoder.
Table: Offset 10h: MXTBA (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
31:15 RW 0 Base Address (BA): Base address of memory space
14 RW/RO 0 Base Address Bit 14 (BAB14): When SATAGC.MSS[1:0]=“00”, this bit is Read Only ‘0’ else it’s Read Write ‘0’.
13 RW/RO 0 Base Address Bit 13 (BAB13): When SATAGC.MSS[1:0]=“00” or “01”, this bit is Read Only ‘0’ else it’s Read Write ‘0’.
12:4 RO 0 Reserved
3 RO 0 Prefetchable (PF): Indicates that this range is not pre-fetchable
2:1 RO 0 Type (TP): Indicates that this range can be mapped anywhere in 32-bit address space
0 RO 0 Resource Type Indicator (RTE): Indicates a request for Memory space.
10.1.1.12 Offset 14h: MXPBA -MSI-X Pending Bit Array Base Address
This BAR is used to allocate 256-byte Memory space for the MSI-X PBA.
NOTE: If Fabric Decoding scheme is used, this register is shadowed by the Fabric Decoder.
Table: Offset 14h: MXPBA (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
31:8 RW 0 Base Address (BA): Base address of memory space (aligned to 256B)
7:4 RO 0 Reserved
3 RO 0 Prefetchable (PF): Indicates that this range is not pre-fetchable
2:1 RO 0 Type (TP): Indicates that this range can be mapped anywhere in 32-bit address space
0 RO 0 Resource Type Indicator (RTE): Indicates a request for Memory space.
10.1.1.13 Offset 18h: SCMDBA - Secondary Command Block Base Address
BAR2 register define a 8-byte I/O space but this space is not implemented. Accesses to this space will get master abort. This space is
created to workaround an issue in RST.
Table: Offset 18h: SCMDBA (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
31:16 RO 0 Reserved
15:3 RW 0 Base Address (BAR): Base address of the I/O space (8 consecutive I/O locations).

10.1.2 Group 0 SAI Policy
G0SAIPOLCTRL and G0SAIPOLAC governs the security policy of the 3 register spaces in SATA, i.e. Config Space, MMIO space and IO
Space. G0SAIPOLCTRL provide the write access to G0SAIPOLAC register and G0SAIPOLCTRL itself. G0SAIPOLAC provide both read
and write access to the 3 register spaces (excluding the G0SAIPOLCTRL and G0SAIPOLAC registers in config space). Each bit in the
G0SAIPOLCTRL and G0SAIPOLAC is associated with the 6-bit SAI Index which is mapped to a particular 8-bit SAI value or values. Refer
to Table: 8-bit SAI Value mapping to 6-bit SAI Index for more detail.
10.1.2.1 Offset 40h: G0SAIPOLCTRL - Group 0 SAI Policy Control
Table: Offset 40h: G0SAIPOLCTRL (source)
Bit Type Reset Description
Group 0 SAI Policy Control (G0SAIPOLCTRL):
Bit wise register where each bit represent the 6-bit SAI Index that mapped to a particular 8-bit SAI value or
values.
A value ‘1’ in this register bit means that a Config Cycle with SAI value that match the mapped 8-bit SAI
G0SAIPOLCTRL_DEFAULT value or values has the write access to the G0SAIPOLCTRL register and G0SAIPOLAC register.
63:0 RW
[63:0] A valuea ‘0’ in this register bit means that a Config Cycle with SAI value that match the mapped 8-bit SAI
value or values has no the write access to the G0SAIPOLCTRL register and G0SAIPOLAC register.
Config Cycle to the SAIPOLCTRL register and SAIPOLAC register always has read access disregard of the
value of this register.
This register is not reset by FLR.
10.1.2.2 Offset 48h: G0SAIPOLAC - Group 0 SAI Policy Access Control
Table: Offset 48h: G0SAIPOLAC (source)
Bit Type Reset Description
Group 0 SAI Policy Access Control (G0SAIPOLAC):
Bit wise register where each bit represent the 6-bit SAI Index that mapped to a particular 8-bit SAI value or
values.
A value ‘1’ in this register bit means that a Cycle with SAI value that match the mapped 8-bit SAI value or
G0SAIPOLAC_DEFAULT
63:0 RW values has both the read and write access to the three register spaces (excluding the G0SAIPOLCTRL and
[63:0]
G0SAIPOLAC registers in the config space).
A value ‘0’ in this register bit means that a Cycle with SAI value that match the mapped 8-bit SAI value or
values does not have both the read and write access to the three register spaces.
This register is not reset by FLR.

No Soft Reset (NSFRST): A ‘1’ indicates that devices transitioning from D3hot to D0 because of PowerState commands do not

3 RO 1 additional operating system intervention is required to preserve configuration context beyond writing to the PowerState bits.

Power State (PS): This field is used both to determine the current power state of the SATA Controller and to set a new power
state. The values are:
00 = D0 state
11 = D3HOT state
1:0 RW 00 When in the D3HOT state, the controller’s configuration space is available, but the I/O and memory spaces are not. Additionally,
interrupts are blocked. If software attempts to write a ‘10’ or ‘01’ to these bits, the write will be ignored.
Refer to PCI PM specification section 8.2.2. on software requirements in ensuring I/O space, memory space and Bus Master
are disabled prior to entering D3 state.

Bit 0: Port 0. This bit is only applicable to project(s) that have port 0 physically.
Software cannot set the PCD[port x]=‘1’ if the corresponding config PCS.PxE=‘1’ or AHCI MMIO GHC.PI[x]=‘1’.
Not for EDS: TM.PCD[x] statically gates clock into a SATA port hardware when set to ‘1’. This renders the port non-functional.
10.1.5.2 Offset 94h: PCS - Port Control and Status
By default, the SATA ports are set (by hardware) to the disabled state (e.g. bits[7:0] == ‘0’) as a result of an initial power on reset. When
enabled by software, the ports can transition between the on, partial, and slumber states and can detect devices. When disabled, the
port is in the ‘off’ state and cannot detect any devices.
NOTE: This register is not reset by FLR. NOTE: AHCI specific notes:
If an AHCI-aware or RAID enabled operating system is being booted then system BIOS shall insure that all supported SATA ports are
enabled prior to passing control to the OS. Once the AHCI aware OS is booted it becomes the enabling/disabling policy owner for the
individual SATA ports. This is accomplished by manipulating a port’s PxSCTL.DET and PxCMD.SUD fields. Because an AHCI or RAID
aware OS will typically not have knowledge of the PxE bits and because the PxE bits act as master on/off switches for the ports, pre-
boot software must insure that these bits are set to ‘1’ prior to booting the OS, regardless as to whether or not a device is currently on
the port.

Port 0 Enabled (P0E):
When RO-zero condition below is true, this bit is reserved and read-only 0.
When set, the port is enabled. When cleared, the port is disabled. When enabled, the port can transition between the on,
partial, and slumber states and can detect devices. When disabled, the port is in the ‘off’ state and cannot detect any
devices.
This bit takes precedence over P0CMD.SUD. BIOS shall program the P0E to ‘1’ prior to starting the AHCI initialization flow.
RW / RO-zero condition:
0 0
RO
MAP.SPD[0] is ‘1’, OR
SATA PORT muxing for port 0 based on fuses, soft straps and GPIO does not select SATA
The recommendation for software code that intends to clear all PCS.PxE bits that are previously ‘1’ to ‘0’ and then to ‘1’
again immediately shall refer to the polling requirement as described in P0P register bit. At any time that BIOS or software
is clearing PCS.PxE from ‘1’ to ‘0’, due to time needed for port staggering hardware process (up to 8 ports) to complete,
BIOS and software shall delay the write to set the TM.PCD register by 1.4μs.
This bit is only applicable to project(s) that have port 0 physically.
10.1.5.3 Offset 9Ch: SATAGC - SATA General Configuration
Table: Offset 9Ch: SATAGC (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
Register Lock (REGLOCK):
BIOS can set this bit to ‘1’ to lock the following registers with RW/L attribute:
CAP,CP, MID.NEXT, PIE.NEXT, SATACR0.NEXT
Once locked the register attribute of above list changes from RW/L to RO holding the existing value.
31 RWO 0 BIOS is required to program this field to ‘1’ prior to handle off to OS. If BIOS needs the SATA host controller to change
operation a few times (i.e. changing CC.SCC mode) and need different capability structures for each specific operation
mode, BIOS need not activate the lock until BIOS is ready to hand off to OS.
BIOS may need to separate write access to this byte offset (x9Fh) from write to the lower 3-byte of the dword (x9C-9Eh) if
there is a need to program the lower 3-byte dword location early during boot process.
This field is not reset by FLR.
Reserved. This field is not reset by FLR.
30:25 RW 0 BIOS may need to separate write access to this byte offset (x9Fh) from write to the lower 3-byte of the dword (x9C-9Eh) if
there is a need to program the lower 3-byte dword location early during boot process.
24:18 RW 0 Reserved. This field is not reset by FLR.
Do_Serr Disable (DOSERRD): When ‘1’, SERR reporting is disabled (DO_SERR Sideband message sending is disabled or
SERR# Wire is supressed. STS.SSE setting is not governed by this policy bit). When ‘0’, SERR reporting is enabled (DO_SERR
17 RW 0
Sideband message sending is enabled or SERR# Wire is not supressed).
This register field is not reset by FLR.
SATA Mode Select (SMS): Software (SW) programs these bits to control the mode in which the SATA HBA should operate:
0b = AHCI mode
1b = RAID mode
SW shall not manipulate SATAGC.SMS during runtime operation; i.e. the OS will not do this. The BIOS may choose to switch
16 RW 0 from one mode to another during POST.
AHCI mode may be selected when RAID feature is enabled by fuse.
RAID mode may only be selected when FFSATA5 and FFSATA3 (concatenated value not indicating “No RAID”).
This register field is not reset by FLR.
If Fabric Decoding scheme is used, this register bit is shadowed by the Fabric Decoder.
Data Phase Parity Error Enable (DPPEE): When ‘1’, IOSF data phase parity error handling is enabled. When ‘0’, the data
15 RW 0 phase parity error handling is disabled.
This register field is not reset by FLR.
Write Request_Size Select / Max_Payload_Size (WRRSELMPS):
These two bits select the max write request size that SATA host controller will initiate for DMA write to memory. SATA host
controller will internally break up larger write request based on these bits. The request is address-aligned to the selected
size.
14:12 RW 000
Defined encodings for this field are:
000b 128 address aligned bytes max payload size111b 64 address aligned bytes max payload size.All other values are
reserved for SATA host controller.
This field is not reset by FLR.
Command Parity Error Enable (CPEE): When ‘1’, command parity error handling is enabled. When ‘0’, the command parity
11 RW 0 error handling is disable.
This field is not reset by FLR.
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 60/242
=== PAGE 61 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
SATA Controller Function Disable (SCFD): BIOS program this bit to ‘1’ to disable the SATA Controller function. When ‘0’,
SATA Controller function is enabled. When disable, SATA Host Controller will not claimed the register access targeting its
Configuration Space. In IOSF primary Fabric Decode scheme, it’s expected BIOS also program the corresponding bit used
10 RW 0 by the Fabric Decoder accordingly hence both SATA Host Controller and Fabric Decoder are in sync, and BIOS need to
program this bit before programming the one in Fabric Decoder. Once this bit is set, BIOS is not able to revert it back to
Function Enable until next round of platform reset.
This register field is not reset by FLR.
Unsupported Request Reporting Enable (URRE): If set to 1 by software, it allows reporting of an Unsupported Request as a
system error.
9 RW 0
If both URRE and PCI configuration SERR# Enable registers are set to a ‘1’, then the agent must set the Signaled System
Error bit in the PCI Status register and send a DO_SERR message in IOSF-SB interface.
Unsupported Request Detected (URD): Set to ‘1’ by hardware upon detecting an Unspported Request on IOSF Primary
8 RWC 0 interface that is not considered Advisory Non-Fatal. Cleared to ‘0’ by SW.
URD bit is only set based on IOSF primary bus interface activity. It’s not set based on IOSF sideband bus interface activity.
Alternate ID Enable (AIE): When programmed to ‘0’, HW will report the DID value to load the Windows_InBox_Driver. When
programmed to a ‘1’, SATA Host Controller will not report the DID value to load the Windows_InBox_Driver. For more
information, see section 10.1.1.5, Offset 09h: PI Programming Interface, for desktop SKUs and for mobile SKUs for
resultant DIDs.
Programming this bit to a ‘1’ will prevent the Windows in-box version of the Intel AHCI driver from loading on the platform -
will require that the user perform an ‘F6’ install of the Intel driver that is appropriate for the reported DID.
7 RWO 0
This field is applicable when the AHCI is configured for RAID mode of operation. It has no impact for AHCI modes of
operation.
NOTE: BIOS is recommended to program this bit prior to programming the SATAGC.SMS field to reflect RAID.
This field is reset by PLTRST# and BIOS is required to reprogram the value (either ‘0’ or ‘1’) after resuming from S3, S4 or
S5. This insures that the value is properly and cannot be changed during runtime.
This field is not reset by FLR.
AIE0 DevID Selection (DEVIDSEL):
This register allows BIOS to select Device ID when AIE=0 and Server Feature (SATA AIE DEVIDSEL) Disable Fuse=0. This bit
only has effect in Desktop SKU. In Mobile SKU this bit has no effect at all. Refer to config register offset 09h PI for usage.
RWO / Server BIOS is required to program this field to ‘1’ together with the write to the AIE bit in a single configuration write cycle.
6 0
RO Client BIOS is required to program this bit to ‘0’ together with the write to the AIE bit in a single configuration write cycle.
When Server Feature (SATA AIE DEVIDSEL) Disable Fuse is programmed to 1, this disables the writeability of this DEVIDSEL
register bit, and becomes RO with a value of 0.
This field is not reset by FLR.
FLR Capability Selection (FLRCSSEL):
This allows the FLR Capability to be bypassed. Refer to config offset B0h. BIOS is required to program this bit to ‘1’ and
5 RWO 0
config offset A8h SATACR0.NEXT to 00h.
This field is not reset by FLR.

MSI-X Enable (MXE): If set to ‘1’ and the MSI Enable bit in the MSI Message Control register is cleared to ‘0’, the function is

Port 7 BIST FIS Initiate (P7BFI): When a rising edge is detected on this bit, the SATA controller will initiate a BIST FIS to the
device on port 7, using the parameters specified in this register and BFTD1 and BFTD2. The BIST FIS will only be initiated if a
device is present and not in the partial or slumber states. After a BIST FIS is successfully completed, software must disable
17 RW 0 and re-enable the PCS.P7E prior to attempting additional BIST FISes or to return the SATA controller to a normal operational
mode. If the BIST FIS fails, as indicated by BFF in this register, software can clear and then set this bit to initiate another BIST
FIS.
This bit is only applicable to project(s) that have port 7 physically.
Port 6 BIST FIS Initiate (P6BFI): When a rising edge is detected on this bit, the SATA controller will initiate a BIST FIS to the
device on port 6, using the parameters specified in this register and BFTD1 and BFTD2. The BIST FIS will only be initiated if a
device is present and not in the partial or slumber states. After a BIST FIS is successfully completed, software must disable
16 RW 0 and re-enable the PCS.P6E prior to attempting additional BIST FISes or to return the SATA controller to a normal operational
mode. If the BIST FIS fails, as indicated by BFF in this register, software can clear and then set this bit to initiate another BIST
FIS.

10.3 Memory Registers
10.3.1 AHCI Memory Registers
All of the AHCI memory mapped registers are in the core well, unless stated otherwise. The memory mapped registers within the SATA
controller exist in non-cacheable memory space. Additionally, locked accesses are not supported. If software attempts to perform
locked transactions to the registers, indeterminate results may occur. Register accesses shall have a maximum size of 64 bits. 64 bit
accesses must not cross an 8 byte alignment boundary.
The registers are divided into two sections - global control registers and port control registers. All registers that start below address
100h are global and meant to apply to the entire HBA. The port control registers are the same for all ports, and there are as many
registers banks as there are ports.
All registers not defined and all reserved bits within registers return ‘0’ when read.
When SATA host controller entering IP Accessible power gating state, all Memory registers context are kept unless specified otherwise
explicitly. Memory registers where its context is not kept are reset.

Start End Description

28h 5Fh Reserved
60h 9Fh Reserved.

D0h FFh Reserved
100h 17Fh Port 0 port control registers
180h 1FFh Port 1 port control registers
200h 27Fh Port 2 port control registers
280h 2FFh Port 3 port control registers
300h 37Fh Port 4 port control registers
380h 3FFh Port 5 port control registers
400h 47Fh Port 6 port control registers

500h 57Fh Reserved

580h 587h Enclosure Management for more information. These locations are reserved if enclosure
management is not supported (i.e. GHC_CAP.EMS = 0).

10.3.1.1.2 Offset 04h: GHC - Global HBA Control
This register controls various global actions of the HBA.
Table: Offset 04h: GHC (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
AHCI Enable (AE): When set, indicates that an AHCI driver is loaded and communication to the HBA shall be via AHCI
mechanisms. This can be used by an HBA that supports both legacy mechanisms (such as SFF-8038i) and AHCI to know when
the HBA is running under an AHCI driver.
When set, software shall only talk to the HBA using AHCI. The HBA will not have to allow command processing via both AHCI
31 RO 1 and legacy mechanisms. When cleared, software will only communicate with the HBA using legacy mechanisms. Software
shall set this bit to ‘1’ before accessing other AHCI registers.
The implementation of this bit is dependent upon the value of the GHC_CAP.SAM bit. If GHC_CAP.SAM is ‘0’, then GHC.AE
should be RW and shall have a reset value of ‘0’. If GHC_CAP.SAM is ‘1’, then AE shall be readonly and shall have a reset value of
‘1’.
30:3 RO 0 Reserved
MSI Revert to Single Message (MRSM): When set to ‘1’ by hardware, indicates that the HBA requested more than one MSI
vector but has reverted to using the first vector only. When this bit is cleared to ‘0’, the HBA has not reverted to single MSI mode
(i.e. hardware is already in single MSI mode, software has allocated the number of messages requested, or hardware is sharing
interrupt vectors if MC.MME < MC.MMC).
The HBA may revert to single MSI mode when the number of vectors allocated by the host is less than the number requested.
This bit shall only be set to ‘1’ when the following conditions hold:
MC.MSIE = ‘1’ (MSI is enabled)
MC.MMC > 0 (multiple messages requested)
2 RO 0 MC.MME > 0 (more than one message allocated)
MC.MME != MC.MMC (messages allocated not equal to number requested)
When this bit is set to ‘1’, single MSI mode operation is in use and software is responsible for clearing bits in the IS register to
clear interrupts.
This bit shall be cleared to ‘0’ by hardware when any of the four conditions stated is false. This bit is also cleared to ‘0’ when
MC.MSIE = ‘1’ and MC.MME = 0h. In this case, the hardware has been programmed to use single MSI mode, and is not
“reverting” to that mode.
The HBA shall always revert to single MSI mode when the number of vectors allocated by the host is less than the number
requested.
Interrupt Enable (IE): This global bit enables interrupts from the HBA. When cleared (reset default), all interrupt sources from all
1 RW 0
ports are disabled. When set, interrupts are enabled.
HBA Reset (HR): When set by SW, this bit causes an internal reset of the HBA. All state machines that relate to data transfers
and native command queuing will return to an idle condition, and all ports will be re-initialized via COMRESET.
0 RW1 0
When the HBA has performed the reset action, it will reset this bit to ‘0’. A software write of ‘0’ will have no effect. For a
description on which bits are reset when this bit is set, see the AHCI specification, section 10.3.3.

10.3.1.1.5 Offset 10h: VS - AHCI Version
This register indicates the major and minor version of the AHCI specification. It is BCD encoded. The upper two bytes represent the
major version number, and the lower two bytes represent the minor version number. Example: Version 3.12 would be represented as
00030102h.

25 RO 1

10.3.1.2.2 Offset A4h: VS_CAP - Vendor Specific Capabilities Register
Table: Offset A4h: VS_CAP (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
31:28 RO 0 Reserved
NVM Remapped Memory Offset (NRMO):
Specifies the offset (in 128B unit) within ABAR as to where the NVM Remap memory BAR register space is remapped. For
example, NRMO=1 means ABAR + 128B. This allows the remapped offset to shift between ABAR + 0B, and ABAR + 512KK -
128B, with 128B step.
The remapped offset into the AHCI memory space must not overlap with the memory space used for SATA.
27:16 RWO 10h
The remapped offset into the AHCI memory space and the remapped size must not exceed the allocated AHCI memory space
of the integrated AHCI controller.
Only valid when PNMBRE = “1‟. The reset default of this field is 10h, this places the start of the NVM Remap memory BAR
register space at ABAR + 2K.
This field is not reset by FLR.
15:13 RO 0 Reserved
Memory Space Limit (MSL): This field specifies the size (in 128B unit) of the remapped memory space for the NVM Remap
device. It is a 0-based field. For example, MSL=1 means 256B. This allows the remapped size to shift between 128B and 512K
with the step of 128B.
Memory BAR offset from 0 to MSL of the NVM Remap device are remapped under the integrated AHCI controller memory
space.
12:1 RW0 16Fh
The remapped offset into the AHCI memory space and the value programmed in this field must not exceed the allocated AHCI
memory space of the integrated AHCI controller.
Only valid when PNMBRE = “1‟. The reset default of this field is 16Fh which specifies the size of the NVM remapped memory
space as 34K.
This field is not reset by FLR.
NVM Remap Memory BAR Enable (NRMBE):
Set to „1‟ if NVM Remap device is present and remapping of its memory BAR register space is enabled. Cleared to „0‟ if there
0 RWO 0
is no NVM Remap device present or the remapping of its memory BAR register space is disabled.
This bit is not reset by FLR.

Remapping Under NVMe Enable (RUNE)
When set to ‘1’, AHCI Host Controller become a Remapped Device under the NVMe Host Controller hence the Bus Device
Function of AHCI Host Controller is hidden from the OS.
This register is not reset by FLR.
Not for EDS:

Requester ID of DMA cycle from AHCI Host Controller to use the NVMe BDF. Corresponding downstream completion carry the
Requester ID = NVMe BDF.
On PCH PSF side, it use the 2nd instance of SATA Fabric Decoder to route the downstream completion of requester ID of
NVMe BDF based on TAG value..
Config space of AHCI Host Controller is still under the AHCI BDF. SW access (SW Option) or CRn access (HW option) to AHCI
Host Controller config space should target AHCI BDF. Corresponding upstream completion carry the Completer ID = AHCI
16 RWO 0
BDF. Upstream completion correspond to downstream MMIO and IO request also carry the Completer ID = AHCI BDF.

Interface Communication Control (ICC): This field is used to control power management states of the interface. If the Link
layer is currently in the L_IDLE state, writes to this field shall cause the HBA to initiate a transition to the interface power
management state requested. If the Link layer is not currently in the L_IDLE state, writes to this field shall have no effect.
Value Definition
**Reserved
DEVSLP**: This shall cause the HBA to assert the DEVSLP signal associated with the port; the HBA shall ignore the
DEVSLP Idle Timeout value specified by PxDEVSLP.DITO. Software shall only request DEVSLP when the interface is
Fh - in an idle state (i.e. PxCI is cleared to 0h and PxSACT is cleared to 0h); if the interface is not idle at the time the
9h8h register is written, then the HBA takes no action and the interface remains in its current state. If PxGHC_
CAP2.DESO is set to ‘1’ and PxSSTS.IPM is not set to ‘6h’, then the HBA takes no action and the interface remains
in its current state. Additionally, the HBA shall not assert the DEVSLP signal until PHYRDY has been achieved (after
a previous de-assertion).
7h Reserved
Slumber: This shall cause the HBA to request a transition of the interface to the Slumber state. The SATA device
6h
may reject the request and the interface shall remain in its current state.
5h -
31:28 RW 0h Reserved
3h
Partial: This shall cause the HBA to request a transition of the interface to the Partial state. The SATA device may
2h
reject the request and the interface shall remain in its current state.
Active: This shall cause the HBA to request a transition of the interface into the active state. If the requested
1h transition is from the DEVSLP state, then the HBA shall wait until PxDEVSLP.DMAT has expired before de-asserting
the DEVSLP signal.
No-Op/Idle: When software reads this value, it indicates the HBA is ready to accept a new interface control
0h
command, although the transition to the previously selected state may not yet have occurred.
When system software writes a non-reserved value other than No-Op (0h), the HBA shall perform the action and update this
field back to Idle (0h).
If software writes to this field to change the state to a state the link is already in (i.e. interface is in the active state and a
request is made to go to the active state), the HBA shall take no action and return this field to Idle. If the interface is in a low
power state and the software wants to transition to a different low power state, software must first bring the link to active
and then initiate the transition to the desired low power state (with the exception of DEVSLP). The transition to DEVSLP
may occur from any other state if GHC_CAP2.DESO is cleared to ‘0’. If GHC_CAP2.DESO is set to ‘1’, then DEVSLP may only
be transitioned to if the link is in Slumber.
Aggressive Slumber/Partial (ASP): When set to ‘1’, and the ALPE bit is set, the HBA shall aggressively enter the Slumber
state when it clears a bit in the PxCI or PxSACT register and the register values are then PxCI = 0h and PxSACT = 0h. When
27 RW 0 cleared, and the ALPE bit is set, the HBA will aggressively enter the Partial state when it clears a bit in the PxCI or PxSACT
register and the register values are then PxCI = 0h and PxSACT = 0h. If GHC_CAP.SALP is cleared to ‘0’, software shall treat
this bit as reserved.
Aggressive Link Power Management Enable (ALPE): When set, the HBA will aggressively enter a lower link power state
(Partial or Slumber) based upon the setting of the ASP bit. Software shall only set this bit to ‘1’ if GHC_CAP.SALP is set to
26 RW 0
‘1’; if GHC_CAP.SALP is cleared to ‘0’ software shall treat this bit as reserved.
BIOS is recommended to program this field to ‘1’.
Drive LED on ATAPI Enable (DLAE): When set, the HBA will drive the LED pin active for commands regardless of the state of
25 RW 0 PxCMD.ATAPI. When cleared, the HBA will only drive the LED pin active for commands if PxCMD.ATAPI is set to ‘0’. This bit
is set by software.
Device is ATAPI (ATAPI): When set, the connected device is an ATAPI device. This bit is used by the HBA to control whether
24 RW 0
or not to generate the desktop LED when commands are active.
Automatic Partial to Slumber Transitions Enabled (APSTE): When set to ‘1’, the HBA may perform Automatic Partial to
Slumber Transitions. When cleared to ‘0’ the port shall not perform Automatic Partial to Slumber Transitions. Software shall
23 RW 0
only set this bit to ‘1’ if GHC_CAP2.APST is set to ‘1’; if GHC_CAP2.APST is cleared to ‘0’ software shall treat this bit as
reserved.
22 RO 0 FIS-based Switching Capable Port (FBSCP): The SATA controller does not support FIS-Based Switching.
External SATA Port (ESP): When set to ‘1’, indicates that this port is routed externally and will be used with an external SATA
device. When set to ‘1’, GHC_CAP.SXS must also be set to ‘1’. When cleared (‘0’), indicates that this port is not routed
21 RWO 0
externally and supports internal SATA devices only. If ESP is set to ‘1’, then the port may experience hot plug events.
This bit is not reset on a HBA reset.
20 RO 0 Cold Presence Detection (CPD): The SATA controller does not support cold presence detect.
Mechanical Presence Switch Attached to Port (MPSP): If set to ‘1’, the platform supports a mechanical presence switch
attached to this port. If cleared to ‘0’, the platform does not support a mechanical presence switch attached to this port.
When this bit is set to ‘1’, PxCMD.HPCP should also be set to ‘1’.
19 RWO 0
The HBA takes no action on the state of this bit - it is for system software only. For example, if this bit is cleared, and an
interlock switch toggles, the HBA shall still treat it as a proper interlock switch event.
Note that this bit is not reset on a HBA reset.
Hot Plug Capable Port (HPCP): This indicates whether the port is connected to a device which can be hot plugged. SATA by
definition is hot-pluggable, but not all platforms are constructed to allow the device to be removed (it may be screwed into
the chassis, for example). This bit can be used by system software to indicate a feature such as “eject device” to the end-
18 RWO 0 user.
The HBA takes no action on the state of this bit - it is for system software only. For example, if this bit is cleared, and a hot
plug event occurs, the HBA shall still treat it as a proper hot plug event.
This bit is not reset on a HBA reset.
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 79/242
=== PAGE 80 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
Port Multiplier Attached (PMA): When set, a Port Multiplier is attached to the HBA for this port. When cleared, a Port
17 RW/RO 0 Multiplier is not attached to the HBA for this port. This bit is a read only ‘0’ when GHC_CAP.SPM = ‘0’, and read/write when
GHC_CAP.SPM = ‘1’. Note that this bit is set by software; hardware does not auto-detect that a Port Multiplier is attached.
16 RO 0 Reserved
15 RO 0 Command List Running (CR): When this bit is set it indicates that the command list DMA engine for the port is running.
FIS Receive Running (FR): When this bit is set it indicates that the FIS Receive DMA engine for the port is running.
14 RO 0 Note to software: When FR bit stays set, read the PxIS.PCS and PxSERR.DET.X to service the PCS interrupt
accordingly if any.
Mechanical Presence Switch State (MPSS): The MPSS bit reports the state of a mechanical presence switch attached to
See this port. If GHC_CAP.SMPS is set to ‘1’ and the mechanical presence switch is closed then this bit is cleared to ‘0’. If GHC_
13 RO
Desc CAP.SMPS is set to ‘1’ and the mechanical presence switch is open then this bit is set to ‘1’. If GHC_CAP.SMPS is set to ‘0’
then this bit is cleared to ‘0’. Software should only use this bit if both GHC_CAP.SMPS and PxCMD.MPSP are set to ‘1’.
Current Command Slot (CCS): Indicates the current command slot the HBA is processing. This field is valid when the
PxCMD.ST bit is set, and is constantly updated by the HBA. This field can be updated as soon as the HBA recognizes an
active command slot, or at some point soon after when it begins processing the command. When PxCMD.ST transitions
12:8 RO 0h from a ‘1’ to a ‘0’, the HBA will reset this field to ‘0’. After PxCMD.ST transitions from ‘0’ to ‘1’, the highest priority slot to
issue from next is command slot 0. After the first command has been issued, the highest priority slot to issue from next is
PxCMD.CCS + 1. For example, after the HBA has issued its first command, if PxCMD.CCS = 0h and PxCI is set to 3h, the
next command that will be issued is from command slot 1.
7:5 RO 0 Reserved
FIS Receive Enable (FRE): When set, the HBA may post received FISes into the FIS receive area pointed to by PxFB and
PxFBU. When cleared, received FISes are not accepted by the HBA, except for the first D2H register FIS after the
initialization sequence.
4 RW 0
System software must not set this bit until PxFB and PxFBU have been programmed with a valid pointer to the FIS receive
area. If software wishes to move the base, this bit must first be cleared, and software must wait for the PxCMD.FR bit to be
cleared before updating PxFB and PxFBU. Software must not clear this bit while PxCMD.ST is set to ‘1’.
Command List Override (CLO): Setting this bit to ‘1’ causes PxTFD.STS.BSY and PxTFD.STS.DRQ to be cleared to ‘0’. This
allows a software reset to be transmitted to the device regardless of whether the BSY and DRQ bits are still set in the
PxTFD.STS register. The HBA sets this bit to ‘0’ when PxTFD.STS.BSY and PxTFD.STS.DRQ have been cleared to ‘0’. A write
3 RW1 0 to this register with a value of ‘0’ shall have no effect.
This bit shall only be set to ‘1’ immediately prior to setting the PxCMD.ST bit to ‘1’ from a previous value of ‘0’. Setting this
bit to ‘1’ at any other time is not supported and will result in indeterminate behavior. Software must wait for CLO to be
cleard to ‘0’ before setting PxCMD.ST to ‘1’.
2 RO 1 Power On Device (POD): The SATA controller does not support cold presence detect.
Spin-Up Device (SUD): This bit is read/write for HBAs that support staggered spin-up via GHC_CAP.SSS. This bit is read only
‘1’ for HBAs that do not support staggered spin-up. On an edge detect from ‘0’ to ‘1’, the HBA shall start a COMRESET
RW/
1 0/1 initialization sequence to the device. Clearing this bit causes no action on the interface. Clearing this bit to ‘0’ does not
RO
cause any OOB signal to be sent on the interface. When this bit is cleared to ‘0’ and PxSCTL.DET = 0h, the HBA will enter
listen mode.
Start (ST): When set, the HBA may process the command list. When cleared, the HBA may not process the command list.
Whenever this bit is changed from a ‘0’ to a ‘1’, the HBA starts processing the command list at entry ‘0’. Whenever this bit is
0 RW 0 changed from a ‘1’ ot a ‘0’, the PxCI and PxSACT register is cleared by the HBA upon the HBA putting the controller into an
idle state. PxTFD shall be updated also.
See section 10.3.1 of the AHCI spec for restrictions on when PxCMD.ST can be set to ‘1’ and cleared to ‘0’.

10.3.1.4.1 Offset 120h, 1A0h, 220h, 2A0h, 320h, 3A0h, 420h, 4A0h: PxTFD - Port [0-7] Task File Data
This is a 32-bit register that copies specific fields of the task file when FISes are received. The FISes that contain this information are:
D2H Register FIS
PIO Setup FIS
Set Device Bits FIS (BSY and DRQ are not updated with this FIS)
Table: Offset 120h, 1A0h, 220h, 2A0h, 320h, 3A0h, 420h, 4A0h: PxTFD (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
31:16 RO 0 Reserved
15:8 RO 0 Error (ERR): Contains the latest copy of the task file error register.
Status (STS): Contains the latest copy of the task file status register. Fields of note in this register that affect AHCI:
Bit Value Description
7 BSY Indicates the interface is busy
06:04:00 N/A Not applicable
7:0 RO 7Fh
3 DRQ Indicates a data transfer is requested
02:01:00 N/A Not applicable
0 ERR Indicates an error during the transfer.
The HBA updates all 8 bits of this register from the received FIS, not just the bits noted above.

This is a 32-bit register that contains the initial signature of an attached device when the first D2H Register FIS is received from that
device. It is updated once after a reset sequence.

10.3.1.4.3 Offset 128h, 1A8h, 228h, 2A8h, 328h, 3A8h, 428h, 4A8h: PxSSTS - Port [0-7] Serial ATA Status
This is a 32-bit register that conveys the current state of the interface and host. The HBA updates it continuously and asynchronously.
When the HBA transmits a COMRESET to the device, this register is updated to its reset values.
Table: Offset 128h, 1A8h, 228h, 2A8h, 328h, 3A8h, 428h, 4A8h: PxSSTS (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
31:12 RO 0 Reserved
Interface Power Management (IPM): Indicates the current interface state:
0h = Device not present or communication not established
1h = Interface in active state
2h = Interface in PARTIAL power management state
6h = Interface in SLUMBER power management state
11:8 RO 0
8h = DEVSLP asserted
All other values reserved.
This field reflects the interface power management state for both device and host initiated power management.
If an Automatic Partial to Slumber Transition occurs, PxSSTS.IPM shall reflect that the host has entered Slumber (PxSSTS.IPM
= ‘6h’)
Current Interface Speed (SPD): Indicates the negotiated interface communication speed.
0h = Device not present or communication not established
1h = Generation 1 communication rate negotiated
7:4 RO 0
2h = Generation 2 communication rate negotiated
3h = Generation 3 communication rate negotiated
All other values reserved
Device Detection (DET): Indicates the interface device detection and Phy state.
0h = No device detected and Phy communication not established
1h = Device presence detected but Phy communication not established
3h = Device presence detected and Phy communication established
4h = Phy in offline mode as a result of the interface being disabled or running in a BIST loopback mode
3:0 RO X
All other values reserved**.
While the true reset default value of this register is 0h, the value read from this register depends on drive presence and the
point in time within the initialization process when the register is read.
The means by which the implementation determines device presence may be vendor specific. However, device presence shall
always be indicated anytime a COMINIT signal is received.”
10.3.1.4.4 Offset 12Ch, 1ACh, 22Ch, 2ACh, 32Ch, 3ACh, 42Ch, 4ACh: PxSCTL - Port [0-7] Serial ATA Control
This is a 32-bit read-write register by which software controls SATA capabilities. Writes to this register result in an action being taken by
the host adapter or interface. Reads from the register return the last value written to it.

Speed Allowed (SPD): Indicates the highest allowable speed of the interface.
0h No speed negotiation restrictions
1h Limit speed negotiation to Generation 1 communication rate
7:4 RW 0h 2h Limit speed negotiation to a rate not greater than Generation 2 communication rate.
3h Limit speed negotiation to a rate not greater than Generation 3 communication rate

If software changes SPD after port has been enabled, software is required to perform a port reset via DET=1h.
Device Detection Initialization (DET): Controls the HBA’s device detection and interface initialization.
**0h No device detection or initialization action requested
1h Perform interface communication initialization sequence to establish communication. This is functionally equivalent to a
hard reset and results in the interface being reset and communications reinitialized. While this field is 1h, COMRESET is
continuously transmitted on the interface. Software should leave the DET field set to 1h for a minimum of 1 millisecond to
3:0 RW 0h ensure that a COMRESET is sent on the interface.
4h Disable the Serial ATA interface and put Phy in offline mode.
All other values reserved.
This field may only be changed when PxCMD.ST is ‘0’. Changing this field while the HBA is running results in undefined
behavior. When PxCMD.ST is set to ‘1’, this field should have a value of 0h.
It is permissible to implement any of the Serial ATA defined behaviors for transmission of COMRESET when PxSCTL.DET = 1h

3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
DITO Multiplier (DM): 0’s based value that specifies the DITO multiplier that the HBA applies to the specified DITO value,
effectively extending the range of DITO from 1ms to 16368ms. A value of 0h indicates a multiplier of 1. A maximum
28:25 RWO Fh multiplier of 16 may be applied. The HBA computes the total idle timeout as a product of DM and DITO (i.e. DITO actual =
DITO * (DM + 1)).
These bits are not reset on an HBA reset.
DEVSLP Idle Timeout (DITO): This field specifies the amount of the time (in approximate 1ms granularity) that the HBA shall
wait before driving the DEVSLP signal.
Hardware reloads its port specific DEVSLP timer with this value each time the port transitions out of DEVSLP state. For
example: from DEVSLP to active or PxDEVSLP.ADSE transitions from ‘0’ to a ‘1’.
24:15 RW/RO 4h
If GHC_CAP2.SDS or GHC_CAP2.SADM or PxDEVSLP.DSP is cleared to ‘0’ then these bits are read-only 0h and software
shall treat these bits as reserved.
Software shall only set this value when PxCMD.ST is cleared to ‘0’ and PxDEVSLP.ADSE is cleared to ‘0’.
These bits are not reset on an HBA reset.
DEVSLP Minimum Assertion Time (MDAT or formerly DMAT): This field specifies the minimum amount of time (in 1ms
granulatity) that the HBA must assert the DEVSLP signal before it may be de-asserted. The norminal value is 10ms and the
minimum is 1ms depending on device identification information.
If GHC_CAP2.SDS is cleared to ‘0’ or PxDEVSLP.DSP is cleared to ‘0’ then these bits are read-only 0h and software shall treat
14:10 RW/RO Ah
these bits as reserved.
Software shall only set this value when PxCMD.ST is cleared to ‘0’, PxDEVSLP.ADSE is cleared to ‘0’., and prior to setting
PxCMD.ICC to 8h.
These bits are not reset on an HBA reset.
DEVSLP Exit Timeout (DETO): This field specifies the maximum duration (in approximate 1ms granularity) from DEVSLP de-
assertion until the device is ready to accept OOB. The norminal value is 20ms while the max value is 255ms depending on
device identification information.
If GHC_CAP2.SDS is cleared to ‘0’ or PxDEVSLP.DSP is cleared to ‘0’ then these bits are read-only 0h and software shall treat
9:2 RW/RO 14h
these bits as reserved.
Software shall only set this value when PxCMD.ST is cleared to ‘0’, PxDEVSLP.ADSE is cleared to ‘0’, and prior to setting
PxCMD.ICC to 8h.
These bits are not reset on a HBA reset.
Device Sleep Present (DSP): If set to ‘1’, the platform supports DEVSLP on this port. If cleared to ‘0’, the platform does not
support DEVSLP on this port. This bit may only be set to ‘1’ if GHC_CAP2.SDS is set to ‘1’.
1 RWO 1 DSP is mutually exclusive with the PxCMD.HPCP bit and PxCMD.ESP bit.
BIOS is required to program this field to ‘1’ if the system supports the DEVSLP feature.
These bits are not reset on a HBA reset.
Aggressive DEVSLP Enable (ADSE): This bit is read/write for HBAs that support aggressive DEVSLP management (GHC_
CAP2. SADM = ‘1’). When this bit is set to ‘1’, the HBA shall assert the DEVSLP signal after the port has been idle (PxCI = 0h
and PxSACT = 0h) for the amount of time specified by the PxDEVSLP.DITO register and the interface is in Slumber
(PxSSTS.IPM = 6h).
When this bit is cleared to ‘0’, the HBA does not enter DEVSLP unless software directed via PxCMD.ICC. This bit shall only
0 RW/RO 0 be set to ‘1’ if PxDEVSLP.DSP is set to ‘1’.
If this bit is set to ‘1’ and software clears the bit to ‘0’, then the HBA shall de-assert the DEVSLP signal if asserted.
These bits are not reset on a HBA reset. BIOS is recommended to program this field to ‘1’ if the system support the DEVSLP
feature.
If GHC_CAP2.SDS is cleared to ‘0’ or GHC_CAP2.SADM is cleared to ‘0’, or if PxDEVSLP.DSP is cleared to ‘0’ then these bits
are read-only 0h and software shall treat these bits as reserved.

10.3.2 MSI-X Memory Registers
All registers not defined and all reserved bits within registers return ‘0’ when read.
All memory registers are reset by FLR unless specified otherwise explicitly.
10.3.2.1 PCI Message Signal Interrupt-X Table
Per PCI spec, software must not modify the Address or Data fields of an entry while it is unmasked. Also, care must be taken when
software is using QW access. For example, if software wishes to mask a currently unmasked entry (without setting the Function Mask
bit), software must set the entry’s Mask bit using a DWORD write to the Vector Control field, since performing a QWORD write to the
Message Data and Vector Control fields might result in the Message Data field being modified before the Mask bit in the Vector Control
field becomes set.
MSI-X Table locates in the memory space specified by BAR0 (MXTBA). The table starting offset ($TSO) of MSI-X Table Entry 0 is
MXT.TO[31:3]&“000”.

10.4 SATA Initialization Registers (SIR)
The following section outlines the indexed registers from the SATA configuration space SIRI (or previously DFTI) and SIRD (or previously
DFTD).
Note for EDS: This whole section should not be disclosed externally.
All SIR registers are in the core well. All registers not mentioned are reserved. All SIR registers are reset by backbone reset only unless
specified otherwise explicitly. Indexes not mentioned are reserved. Access attribute (RO/RWC/RW) is undefined.
When SATA host controller enters an IP Accessible power gating state, all SIR register contexts are kept, unless specified otherwise
explicitly. A SIR register is reset where its context is not kept.
This is previously documented and referred to as SATA DFT registers for design teams or SIR in BIOS/EDS spec.
* When SATA host controller entering IP Accessible power gating state, this SIR register context is not kept.
10.4.1 SIR Index 00h - Loop-back Control Register (LBC01)
This register is reset when SATA host controller enters IP Accessible power gating state.
This register is only applicable to project(s) that have port 0 and 1 physically.
Table: SIR Index 00h (source)
Bit Type Reset Description
15 RW 0 Reserved
BERt Timestamp Enable - Setting this bit will enable the Time Stamp register to count up based on incoming 40-bit raw Rx data.
14 RW 0
Clearing this bit will stop the counting and reset the counter to 0.
13 RW 0 BERt Receive Mode - Setting this bit will enable the Bit-Error-Rate receiver test mode.
12 RW 0 Continuous Functional Loop-back Mode Enable - Setting this bit will enable the continuous functional LB mode.
11 RW 0 Single Burst Functional Loop-back Mode Enable - Setting this bit will enable the single-burst functional LB mode.
Inbound SRAM Output Inhibit Mode - This bit will prevent read data from propagating out of the inbound SRAM, as defined by the
10 RW 0
functional LB modes.
Outbound SRAM Output Inhibit Mode - This bit will prevent read data from propagating out of the outbound SRAM, as defined by
9 RW 0
the functional LB modes.
Loop-back AFE Selection (LAS) - This bit is used to select which AFE is being tested for various functional loop-back modes. A 0 in
this bit selects port-0, while a 1 indicates port 1. When 0, port 0 Link Layer operate in TX mode while port 1 Link Layer operate in Rx
8 RW 0
mode. The port that operate in Rx mode (port N) may received the data from its neighboring port N-1 (if exist) or port N+1 (if exist)
and this selection is indicated by bit LARPDSS.
7 RW 0 8B/10B Transmit Bypass Mode - Setting this bit allows transmit data to bypass the 8B/10B encoding on the transmit path.
6 RW 0 Primitive-Insertion Transmit Bypass Mode - Setting this bit disables primitive insertion on the transmit path.
5 RW 0 Scramble Bypass Mode - Setting this bit will disable the scrambling on transmit path and the de-scrambling on the receive path.
4 RW 0 Digital Loop-Back Mode Enable - Setting this bit will enable digital loop-back, bypassing the AFE.
Loop-back RX Port Data Source Selection (LARPDSS) - This register is used to select the data source for a Rx port. A 0 means
select from port N-1. A 1 means select from port N+1. For example:
When port 0 is an Rx port, the LARPDSS=0 option is reserved.
3 RW 0
When port 0 is an Rx port, the LARPDSS=1 selects the data from port 1.
When port 1 is an Rx port, the LARPDSS=0 selects the data from port 0.
When port 1 is an Rx port, the LARPDSS=1 selects the data from port 2.
2:0 RW 0 Reserved

10.4.11 SIR Index 20h - Loop-back Control Register Port 4,5 (LBC45)
This register is only applicable to project(s) that have port 4 and 5 physically.
Table: SIR Index 20h (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
15 RW 0 Reserved
BERt Timestamp Enable - Setting this bit will enable the Time Stamp register to count up based on incoming 40-bit raw Rx data.
14 RW 0
Clearing this bit will stop the counting and reset the counter to 0.
13 RW 0 BERt Receive Mode - Setting this bit will enable the Bit-Error-Rate receiver test mode.
12 RW 0 Continuous Functional Loop-back Mode Enable - Setting this bit will enable the continuous functional LB mode.
11 RW 0 Single Burst Functional Loop-back Mode Enable - Setting this bit will enable the single-burst functional LB mode.
Inbound SRAM Output Inhibit Mode - This bit will prevent read data from propagating out of the inbound SRAM, as defined by the
10 RW 0
functional LB modes.
Outbound SRAM Output Inhibit Mode - This bit will prevent read data from propagating out of the outbound SRAM, as defined by
9 RW 0
the functional LB modes.
Loop-back AFE Selection (LAS) - This bit is used to select which AFE is being tested for various functional loop-back modes. A 0 in
this bit selects port-4, while a 1 indicates port 5. When 0, port 4 Link Layer operate in TX mode while port 5 Link Layer operate in Rx
8 RW 0
mode. The port that operate in Rx mode (port N) may received the data from its neighboring port N-1 (if exist) or port N+1 (if exist)
and this selection is indicated by bit LARPDSS.
7 RW 0 8B/10B Transmit Bypass Mode - Setting this bit allows transmit data to bypass the 8B/10B encoding on the transmit path.
6 RW 0 Primitive-Insertion Transmit Bypass Mode - Setting this bit disables primitive insertion on the transmit path.
5 RW 0 Scramble Bypass Mode - Setting this bit will disable the scrambling on transmit path and the de-scrambling on the receive path.
4 RW 0 Digital Loop-Back Mode Enable - Setting this bit will enable digital loop-back, bypassing the AFE.
Loop-back RX Port Data Source Selection (LARPDSS) - This register is used to select the data source for a Rx port. A 0 means
select from port N-1. A 1 means select from port N+1. For example:
When port 4 is RX port, LARPDSS=0 will select the data from port 3.
3 RW 0
When port 4 is RX port, LARPDSS=1 will select the data from port 5.
When port 5 is RX port, LARPDSS=0 will select the data from port 4.
When port 5 is RX port, LARPDSS=1 will select the data from port 6.
2:0 RW 0 Reserved

10.4.26 SIR Index 98h - Common Test Mode 1 (CTM1)
Table: SIR Index 98h (source)
Bits Type Reset Description
Speed Negotiation ALIGN Detection FSM Disable (SNADD): When this bit is cleared to ‘0’, the align detection FSM output (in
PLL unit) is used to determine if multiple consecutive ALIGNs have been detected during OOB sequence after D10.2 is sent to
31 RW 0
the device. When this bit is set to ‘1’, the internal D8PLaligedetect signal directly from the DRC (d8unit) is used instead (ICH5
behaviour).
30:24 RW 0 Reserved.
SyncFIFO Exposure Disable (SSD): When this bit is set to ‘1’, the SyncFIFO space availablity exposure to BMU during data-out
23 RW 0 transfers is disabled. BMU can not take into consideration up to 256 byte storage space when making data read requests.
When this bit is set to ‘1’, the RRSSEL field in this register must also be set to 10b (128B).
SRST Watchdog Timer Disable (SWTD): If this bit is set to ‘1’, the watchdog timer that forces a completion to be generated
22 RW 0 despite a failure to complete an H2D Register FIS that modifies SRST bit is disabled. The timer resolution is dependent on the
value of bit 16.
PHY RX Recalibration Enable (PRRE): When this register is ‘1’, PHY RX Recalibration handshake is enabled during OOB where
21 RW 0 SATA Host Controller performs the recalibration handshake after device COMWAKE reception. When this register is ‘0’, PHY
RX Recalibration handshake is disabled during OOB.
Method select to qualify the SyncFIFO space (SFS):
20 RW 0 0 - PRD boundary count (default)
1 - SAFE state machine/ request size tracking
19 RW 0 Reserved.
FIS Retry on RERR Disable (FRRD): When this bit is cleared to ‘0’, SATA Host Controller will retry a non-data FIS that it sent if
that FIS received an R_ERR completion status from the device. When this bit is set to ‘1’, the SATA Host Controller will not retry
18 RW 0
a non-data FIS that received an R_ERR completion status. This bit affects legacy operation only. AHCI operation is not affected
by this bit.
Fail FIS if BSY/DRQ Clear (FFBDC): This bit controls how the SATA Host Controller reacts if it receives a FIS from the device
17 RW 0 while both BSY and DRQ bits are cleared to ‘0’. If this bit is set to ‘1’, the SATA Host Controller will respond with an R_ERR
completion status. If this bit is cleared to ‘0’, the SATA SIP will not respond with R_ERR.
Command FIS Watchdog Timer Test Mode (WTTM): The SATA Host Controller contains a watchdog timer for failed Command
FIS transmissions, to ensure that a device or interface failure cannot cause a system hang by preventing an I/O completion.
16 RW 0
Under normal conditions, when this bit is ‘0’, the watchdog timer forces a completion to be returned after 100 ms. In test
mode, when this bit is ‘1’, the watchdog timer forces a completion to be returned after 10 us.
Enhance Error Handling Select (EEHS):
When ‘1’, data parity error on the downstream completion shall not trigger the system error. Instead this error will trigger
device driver fatal error.
When ‘0’, data parity error on the downstream completion shall trigger the system error.
15 RW/RO 0
If Server Feature (Enhance Error Handling Select) Disable Fuse is “1”, this register will always read “0‟ and is Read-only. The
reset value of this register is”0‟.
Client BIOS is required to program this bit to ‘0’. Server BIOS is required to program this bit to ‘1’.
When Server Feature (Enhance Error Handling Select) Disable Fuse is ‘1’, this register bit becomes read only zero.
BERT Error Injection Enable (BEIE): This bit affects BERT and Continuous loopback test modes only. When operating on either
of these modes, error injection is controlled as follows:
When set, the compare logic will force a miscompare (error reported and LBS error status set) every time the BERT timestamp
14 RW 0
counter rolls over.
When cleared, the compare logic will never force miscompares. Error will only be reported when the sampled incoming data
does not match data in the compare buffer.
13 RW 0 Reserved
