25.2.7.2 Parity Generation on IOSF Upstream Interface
VRunit and VSunit always generate a good command parity and data parity for all of its upstream cycles.
The parity generation is independent of parity error detected in the controller internal RX data path. For example: RF parity error,
LMRXFIFO parity error, or SATA CRC error.
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 233/242
=== PAGE 234 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
25.2.7.3 Soft Parity Error
The following modes are supported:
AHCI DMA Data-Out
AHCI PIO Data-Out
AHCI DMA Data-In
AHCI PIO Data-In
The objective of soft parity error handling is to ensure that the corrupted data in RF (due to gamma collision or other reasons) and Link
Layer LMA FIFO do not silently slip through, but are reported to the SW.
In SATA, this is reported to SW via the existing Fatal Error reporting scheme defined in AHCI (PxIS.IFS, PxIS.HBDS). We do not report via
any of the PCI STS bits, like the DPE bit.
For the Link Layer LMA FIFO that transacts FISes, that can be Data FIS or Non-DATA FIS, there is a difference in how these are handled.
FIS Tx always has the CRC inverted such that the Transport layer sets the fatal error bit when Data FIS is R_ERR by the device. For non-
Data FIS, the Transport layer retries.
On Rx, a soft parity error in the LMA FIFO is handled by the Link layer as if it were a CRC error and indicates this to the Transport layer.
Depending on the type of FIS, the Transport layer reacts to the soft parity error: for a Data FIS, it sets the fatal error bit, while for a non-
Data FIS, it is retried by the device.
25.2.7.3.1 Mechanism
FIS Transmission
1. Sparity_Error detected on BMU SRAM output sets the existing parity error indicator from BMU to DMA and finally propagates to LINK.
2. Sparity_Error detected on BMU SRAM output sets the PxSERR.E immediately.
3. Sparity_Error detected on syncFIFO SRAM output sets the existing parity error indicator from MUX to LMA.
4. Sparity_Error detected on syncFIFO SRAM output sets the PxSERR.E immediately.
5. Sparity_Error detected on LMA TX FIFO output sets the existing parity error indicator from LMA to LINK.
6. Sparity_Error detected on LMA TX FIFO output sets the PxSERR.E immediately.
7. Link will invert the CRC. For Data FIS, this causes the device to R_ERR and return RD2H with the ERR bit set. HBA sets PxSERR.H=1
and PxIS.IFS=1 when it see R_ERR on DH2D and this stop the DMA and report/MSI to the SW. For Non-Data FIS, this causes the
device to R_ERR, and the host will retry the FIS transmission again. HBA sets PxSERR.H=1 and PxIS.INFS=1 when it sees R_ERR on
RH2D. This does not stop the DMA.
8. For Data FIS, even though an Sparity_Error is detected, it will not be reported to the SW and stop the DMA immediately. It will only be
reported to the SW and stop the DMA at the end of the DH2D.
9. For Data FIS, when the DMA stops and the SW sees:
PxIS.TFES set by device’s RD2H
The PxCMD.CCS points to the CI that has the Sparity_Error, and that CI bit is not cleared
The last updated BCU value should not count the data that has the Sparity_Error
FIS Reception
1. An Sparity_Error detected on the BMU SRAM output sets the PxIS.HBDS immediately. The HBDS definition includes a data write to
system memory, as well.
2. An Sparity_Error detected on the BMU SRAM output sets the PxSERR.E immediately.
3. An Sparity_Error detected on the syncFIFO SRAM output sets the PxIS.HBDS immediately.
4. An Sparity_Error detected on the syncFIFO SRAM output sets the PxSERR.E immediately.
5. An Sparity_Error detected on the LMA RX FIFO output is handled as if it is a Link Layer CRC error, which sets the PxSERR.C bit and
PxIS.IFS (for Data FIS) and PxIS.INFS (for Non-Data FIS) bit at the end of the FIS reception, along with the Link Layer generating a
R_ERR to the RX FIS.
6. An Sparity_Error detected on the LMA RX FIFO output sets the PxSERR.E immediately.
7. PxIS.HBDS=1 or PxIS.IFS=1 stops the DMA and reports/MSI to theSW. PxIS.INFS=1 does not stop the DMA.
8. For Data FIS, when an Sparity_Error is detected, it is reported to SW and stops the DMA immediately. If the 1st data from the
syncFIFO has an Sparity_Error, the DMA can stop even before any data is posted to memory, or before the PRD info is available. For a
Non-Data FIS, when an Sparity_Error is detected, it is reported to SW but does not stop the DMA. Instead, the device will retry the
Non-Data FIS after receiving an R_ERR from the host.
9. For a Data FIS, when the DMA stops, the SW sees the following:
a. PxIS.HBDS set by HBA
b. The PxCMD.CCS that is pointing to the CI has an Sparity_Error, and that CI bit is not cleared
c. The last updated BCU value should not count the data that has the Sparity_Error.
25.2.8 SATA PORT Lane MUXing
Two usages for the per port 2-bit fuse and 2-bit soft-strap for SATA PORT lane MUXing are as follows:
MOD-PHY Lane Ownership selection based on fuse/soft-strap/satagp:
MOD-PHY Lane is owned by SATA if the below is true, otherwise, the MOD-PHY Lane is NOT owned by SATA:
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 234/242
=== PAGE 235 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
Fuse = “statically select SATA” or
Fuse = “refer to soft-strap”, AND soft-strap = “statically select SATA” or
Fuse = “refer to soft-strap”, AND soft-strap = “refer to satagp”, AND satagp = “1”.
SATAGP pin usage selection based on fuse/soft-strap:
SATAGP pin is used for MOD-PHY Lane Ownership selection if the condition below is true, otherwise the SATAGP pin is used for
Mechanical Switch:
Fuse = “refer to soft-strap”, AND soft-strap = “refer to satagp”. NOTE: When the SATAGP pin is used for MOD-PHY Lane Ownership
selection, the SATAGP pin is tied off as ‘0’ in the Mechanical Switch logic.
25.2.9 pmc_cs2 Usage
The pmc_cs2 acts as an sosc_clk ungate signal to SATA SIP. When set to ‘0’ it means sosc_clk ungate, that is, SATA SIP never drops the
sosc_clkreq (output from SATA SIP to the SoC).
There are three possible usages of pmc_cs2 (as an input to SATA SIP):
The SoC hard ties it to ‘1’. SATA SIP drives the sosc_clkreq per SATA SIP local conditions. When it detects no usages of sosc_clk, then
it drops the sosc_clkreq to ‘0’ as soon as possible.
The SoC ties it to a register bit that defaults to ‘1’. SATA SIP drives the sosc_clkreq per SATA SIP local conditions. When it detects no
usages of sosc_clk, then it drops the sosc_clkreq to ‘0’ as soon as possible. If there is a bug on sosc_clk gating such that sosc_clkack
from PMC does not work correctly, then the PMC programs that register bit to ‘0’ and SATA SIP always keeps the sosc_clkreq at ‘1’.
The SoC drives it dynamically, such that pmc_cs2 stays at ‘0’ to keep the SATA SIP output sosc_clkreq at ‘1’ even if SATA SIP has
achieved ALL other local sosc_clk gating conditions. Keep it at ‘0’, that is, until the platform has achieved the deepest PM state. This is
the delay effect that occurs while going down to the deepest PM state. For going up, since the SoC exits from the deepest PM state
earlier than SATA SIP, the pmc_cs2 will drop to ‘0’ before SATA SIP locally detects the wake event to assert its sosc_clkreq. This is the
earliest wake effect that occurs during going up.
The SoC can pick the usage it wants.
25.2.10 SATA PME# in VNNAON (BXT-P)
In BXT-P, SATA Sits in VNNAON and it has a local PGD, i.e the gated VNNAON. This local PGD in SATA SIP is power gated during SATA
D3 state. BXT-P SoC allow its VNN power well to be gated (i.e. VNN removal) as well when SATA SIP is in D3 state. Before the support
of BXT-P PCR 1202840273 SATA wake sequence, the logic that that assert the PME event due to SATAGP toggling, sits in the PGD. BXT-
P has the PCR filed to request SATA SIP to assert the PME# in VNNAON domain without waking up the SATA VNNAON gated. There is a
dead lock problem in BXT-P SoC if SATA were to wake up its VNNAON gated well first prior to asserting the PME#. The dead lock
happen because the powering up of SATA VNNAON gated domain require a wake up of the VNN domain to runs its PLL to supply the
prim_clk and side_clk to SATA SIP. When SATA SIP wake up its VNNAON gated domain, it trigger the Chassis Power Management
standard signal like ip_pmc_pg_req_b. But this signal is not the standard signal used in BXT-P to wake up the VNN. The standard signal
used is PME#. The PCR is filed for standardization pursued in BXT-P. The flow below is cut and paste from the BXT-P PCR 1202840273
SATA wake sequence (written by Siang Lin and Michael Klinglesmith).
SATA supports wake on either edge of the “sata_gp” input. The sata_gp input comes from a GPIO input routed as a native function to
the SATA IP.
The flow documented below can start if the System is in S0 or S0ix. From S0ix the PMC must return the system to S0 before the SATA
flow can complete.
The flow is NOT supported from Sx (S3, S4, S5). It is a software responsibility to ensure the System does not enter Sx when SATA is
configured for wake. The SATA HW informs the software of this by indicating in the POWERCAPID.PME_SUPPORT register field (bits
31:27 5’b01000) that wake from D3hot is supported but wake from D3cold is NOT supported. (Note also that PMCSR.PMEE must be set
to generate PME#).
The SATA flow is defined, followed by the PMC behavior, followed by a SoC requirements section.
SATA WAKE from D3 flow
Upon detecting an edge on the sata_gp input the SATA controller behaves as follows:
NOTE: This flow is the same for SATA if the SoC is in S0ix (VNN off) or S0. NOTE: SATA only ever generates a PME from D3hot. *
Asserts clock_req for the sosc_clk clock trunk, and waits for clock ack. * Determines if a wake event (PME) is required, based software
configuration of the controller. (i.e. PMCSR.PMEE is ‘0’ or ‘1’)
Two possible scenarios from here: Wake Required and Wake Not Required.
Wake Required
If a wake is required SATA IP asserts the PME wire.
SATA controller will exit IP Accessible PG state due to the wake by sata_gp. This flow will not complete until VNN is restored, as
the SATA controller will request clocks routed on VNN. This delay is okay.
SATA re-enter IP-Accessible if software does not move it from D3 before the hysteresis time out occurs.
Wake Not Required
If a wake is not required SATA IP won’t asserts the PME wire. Hence no wake to VNN.
VNN stays off. SATA IP will not deassert st_pmc_pgreq_b to wake its own PGD as well.
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 235/242
=== PAGE 236 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
SATA PGD stays power gated. However, SATA IP will still Asserts clock_req for the sosc_clk clock trunk, and waits for clock ack.
SATA IP use the sosc_clk to remember the 1st sata_gp toggling event in its VNNAON well logic. This HW ensure that it doesn’t
lost the HW event. Eventually, when SW come naturally to exit D3 (due to other reason, says, end user want to access the HDD),
SW will find out the sata_gp toggling status bit (SATA Config PMCSR.PMES, AHCI MMIO PxIS.PCS) got set. Those sata_gp
toggling status bit get set by the sosc_clk logic in the VNNAON domain while the SATA PGD remained down.
SATA HW now waits for the system to notify the OS / driver of the PME.
SATA SW will eventually come and query the PCI Config space, this software action will cause the SATA controller to exit IP
Accessible PG state.
PMC response to SATA PME
From Sx
N/A SATA PME will not be enabled in Sx
From S0ix
PMC triggers exit from S0ix
After exit from S0ix PMC sends Assert_IRQn (SCI) interrupt to ITSS (no change normal behavior.) NOTE: Need a PME_STS and
PME_EN bit added in PMC. (see register in acpi.gpe0a_sts/en below).
From S0
PMC sends Assert_IRQn (SCI) interrupt to ITSS.
SoC REQUIREMENTS to support SATA wake flows
The sosc_clk trunk to SATA must be routed as a VNNAON trunk.
The sosc_clk trunk must be derrived from the CRO
The CRO must be available to respond to clock req from SATA in S0ix with no dependence on VNN.
The SATA PME wire must be routed on VNNAON from SATA to PMC.
The GPIOs that provides the SATA.GP input wires to the SATA SIP must be configured in native input mode during IO Standby. NOTE:
There is a one SATA GP pin for each SATA port. Either can trigger a wake. There is only one PME wire from SATA. The GPIOs with the
SATA_GP functionality are GPIO_22, and GPIO_23. NOTE: The BXTp POR S0ix exit latency for a combine ramp Vnn/Vccram is 2.9ms in
BXTp. Note that this doesn’t include the latency for the FW/SW S0ix exit flows in the SoC, which approaches a combined total of 5ms.
There are no conflicts with this system implementation and the SATA wake latency requirements.
Table: acpi.gpe0a_sts (source)

set, and the system is in an S0 state, then the setting of the SATA PMESTS bit will generate an SCI (or SMI# if SCI_EN is not set but
17 RW/1C 1’b0
GLB_SMI_EN is). This bit is cleared by a software write of ‘1’.

25.2.11 ResetPrep
Prior to platform reset (Warm Reset or go Sx), SATA SIP is expected to power down its PGD per Chassis Power Management. Before
powering down its PGD, SATA SIP ensure that it has put the PIPE interface into PS2-Reset state and deassert the pgreq signal to
ModPHY to allow ModPHY to power gate, i.e. SATA SIP prepare the PIPE interface for ModPHY power gate. SATA SIP preparation for
the PIPE interface power gate can be triggered by four sources below.
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 236/242
=== PAGE 237 ===
3/16/26, 4:16 PM SATA 3.0 Controller
No port populated. BIOS keep the port in port disable state, i.e. PIPE interface power gate state.
Device D3 state. ACPI kee the port in port offline state, i.e. PIPE interface power gate state.
SATA SIP receive ResetPrep Sideband message. SATA SIP force the port into offline state, i.e. PIPE interface power gate state.
SATA SIP receive ForcePwrGatePOK Sideband message. SATA SIP force the port into offline state, i.e. PIPE interface power gate state.
FIA is another SIP that sits on the PIPE interface between SATA SIP and ModPHY. It also receive the ForcePwrGatePOK message from
PMC. When it receive that message, it force clock gate and will not be able to pass the PIPE request from SATA SIP to ModPHY. In order
to ensure that SATA SIP had put the PIPE interface into power gated state, PMC has 2 methods to achieve that. PMC choose one.
1. PMC send SATA SIP the ResetPrep message prior to the ForcePwrGatePOK message. When SATA SIP receive the ResetPrep, it
gracefully put the PIPE interface into PS2-Reset state. Later, PMC send ForcePWrGatePOK to both SATA SIP and FIA SIP.
2. PMC doesn’t send ResetPrep to SATA SIP. However, PMC ensure that it send ForcePwrGatePOK to SATA SIP 1st, wait for SATA SIP to
power down, then only issue the ForcePwrGatePOK to FIA SIP.
The issue and discussion that lead to above solution is in attached email below.
In implementation, here is the equation:
If (vb_vp_forcepwrgatepok=1 OR vb_vp_forcepok_only=1) AND (plsatarst_b=0 OR vb_vs_resetprep=1 OR CTM5.IIDPGPP=1), then it
means PIPE is in power gated state.
25.2.12 Gate Count and Area
SATA Estimate Gate Count for SPT-H (8 ports) on p1271.8 process (normalized NAND cell) = 1.25Million gates
SATA Estimate Area for SPT-H on p1271.8 process = 406600 micro-m2
SATA Estimate Gate Count for DNV on p1273.1 process (normalized NAND area = 0.11172 um^2) = 1.36Million gates
SATA Estimate Area for DNV on p1273.1 process = 151,780 micro-m2
Gate and Area estimate excludes Embedded Blocks, such as Register Files.

device concurrently. The power number break down per synthesize-able logic and register file and also categorized into Dynamic power
and Leakage power.

25.3.4 Far-End Retimed Loopback Mode
SATA host controller can enter the far end retimed loopback mode via BIST Activate FIS sent by a SATA device (or test source). This
involves loopback from? the host Rx[port N] to the host Tx [port N] pins. It requires appropriately inserted retiming ALIGN primitives in
the loopback data stream. Refer to the SATA specification for details.
25.3.5 SATA High-Speed-Bypass (HBP)
The SATA High-Speed-Bypass (HBP) mode is used to allow full speed testing to take place on SATA without the PHY.
A bypass in the link-layer allows low-speed data to enter the receiver and for transmit data to be observed at low speeds. This allows a
tester to run cycles that exercise the high-speed (300 MHz) logic without having to drive and sample data at 6 GHz. The entire SATA
Host operates at normal speeds, except for the PHY layer.
Only the SATA Gen3 speed is supported during HBP mode. This mode is activated by setting SIR.SHBP(SHME). SATA HBP is only
activated 1 port at a time. Configurating SIR.SHBP(SHPS) determines which SATA port is in HBP mode.
Figure: DATA Path and Clocks During SATA non-HBP Mode depicts the data/clock structure during non-HBP mode and Figure: DATA
Path and Clocks During SATA SATA HBP Mode depicts the SATA HBP mechanism for comparison.
RX Interface
On the RX interface, a separate data path is created to interface with the SATA link unit instead of the standard PHY data path.
A cross-clock FIFO is in-placed to handle the synchronization of data from the ftc_clk domain to the SATA link clock domain
The ftc_data/ftc_clk is expected to operate at the rate of 40 data bits@125Mhz(500MB/s)
The data and the clock are supplied by NTI in a “double-pump” manner
NTI and its staging flops are SoC-specific and are discussed in this document.
TX Interface
On the TX interface, a SATA CRC block provides 16 bits of CRC results on 40 bits of TXDATA.
The CRC result is observable via SIR.SHBP(SHC).
Setting SIR.SHBP(SHCR) to 1 clears the CRC result to 0.
SHCR is cleared to start the HBP operation.
Figure: DATA Path and Clocks During SATA non-HBP Mode
https://docs.intel.com/documents/pch_doc/CLIP/SATA/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller/Chap25_SATA_Host_Controller.html 241/242
